Another is that you draw out some cause from the membranes; then cut that with an instrument of which this is the form: It is like tweezers, except that the ends of it are curved so that the holes of each of those are in the direction of the other, very sharp, and it should be made of iron heated in vinegar.
But if this instrument is not available to you, then pierce that with vinegar of which this is the form of it: And it should be sharp on one side and blunt on the other.
And after you have pierced one membrane, pierce the other according to this manner of piercing, and then let the patient gargle with water.
But if blood flows out, then gargle with water of decoction of the rind of pomegranate or of bay-leaf and alike to that of the causes astringent until the flow of blood is stopped, and then cure that until it is healed.
And sometimes in the throat there are other abscesses besides those two ears, and you pierce those according to what we have said in the piercing of two membranes equally.
And I had medicated a woman of an abscess which was in her throat; the abscess had turned dark in color, of little feeling, and it had closed up her throat, and she was breathing with difficulty, and she had forbidden herself food and drinking water, and she was coming near to death unless she had stayed for one or two days.
And the abscess had pushed so that it had made two bumps within that they were pus for two months.
So I cut him up with a scalpel and inserted one of them in it, and pulled that out; and there came out of him a great portion, and then I pierced the other side where I understood the other pus was, and then I bound his mouth, and held down his tongue, and then I put the needle in that abscess.
And then I cut away a great part of it, and not much blood flowed out of him. Then the throat of that woman was absolutely open, and she began to drink water at once, and then she ate food; therefore I did not cease to pierce that abscess many times for a long time, and the abscess occurred in the place where that one was, which was prolonged.
Then I cut and cauterized her throat, therefore the addition of that; and then I walked around and did not know what God had done to that; therefore my marvel grew at that.
Chapter 37.
Of the piercing of the navel when it is abscessed.
When there is pus in the navel, and it is abscessed and long, then it is named perpendicular; and if it is thick and round in the lower part, then it is named buba.
But when it is healed with what we have said in the division and does not comply with your cure, and you see that the abscess cauterized is last in him and is subtle; and if it is to that length, and it is blood-red, dark in color or black, and there is no feeling in it, then beware of piercing it, for there is fear over the patient.
And when you see that according to the manner which I have said of its whiteness and length, that you make the patient and press his tongue with the instrument of which I have described the form; and then put the needle in the new one, and pull that down and pierce that with one of two instruments of which I spoke in the piercing of two membranes.
And beware that you do not pierce it unless what is adjusted over the natural term with its addition, for if you pierce further, you will cut his speech.
And after piercing, use what we have recommended in the piercing of two membranes, and cure that until it is healed.
But if the patient is frightened by the piercing of him, beware that you use a needle in cauterizing him without fear, and the manner of the cautery in him is not but with sharp water; then let the head of the patient be in your lap, and then press his tongue with the instrument of which we have spoken, and then take the water which we spoke of in the chapter of cauterization, and comply with that living cause, and pause that not thick nor subtle, and of that fill the concavity of the instrument of which this is the form:
Let the hollow of it be concavity in which is stopped the medicine likewise with the concavity of spoon of rosewater, and pause the instrument with the medicine over the navel; and let the patient jaw over his lap so that run saliva or mouth mucous membrane of that medicine, so that no other cause on the throat of him and that you lead that.
And then hold your hand over the medicine, and squeeze that on the uvula through the space of a half-hour until you see it blackened and subdued by the biting of the medicine.
And if you want, take a needle and wrap that over the end of the rose water; then submerge the needle in the medicine and insert the rosewater into a tube so that the needle adheres in that tube, and do that as many times until you achieve what you want from cauterizing the grape; then let it be blackened as it dries and falls after three or four days.
And if you feel that the medicine should be repeated, repeat it, and then cauterize it by wiping it with a cotton swab dipped in wine, and cleanse it with the water that was used to dissolve the medicine, and wash it with warm water, and treat it from the outside with embrocation, and on the inside with healing remedies until it is healed.
And this kind of treatment is more safe than incision and less painful.
Sometimes, ulcerations of the uvula are healed with something more subtle than cauterization or incision: take myrrh, hyssop, oregano, rue, Arabic thorns, camomile, brot and similar to those herbs, and mix all these ingredients, or some of them, in a bowl, and let them be soaked in mild vinegar; and the bowl should be covered with a decent lid, and there should be a hole in the middle of the lid, on which an appropriate hollow instrument made of silver or brass is placed; it should be fashioned out of silver or brass.
And the end of this instrument is inserted into the mouth of the patient so that the steam reaches the uvula, where it is very fogged up.
And then repeat this process several times until it is dry, and be careful not to perform this treatment during the rising of humors, for it would cause too much pressure on the swelling; instead, wait until the swelling has subsided before cauterizing it.
But if you do not have this instrument at hand, take a reed and attach a ball of wool to its end, so that it fits into the mouth of the patient; for the wool prevents the steam from burning the mouth.
And this treatment is good for health.
Chapter 38.
On the extraction of thorns and other objects that stick in the throat, and on other causes.
Sometimes, there are things stuck in the throat or a thorn from the foot or some other cause.
So you must pull out whatever is visible, using an instrument in front of the tongue, so that it can be seen clearly what is in the throat.
And if there is something hidden in the throat that cannot be seen, the patient should be made to vomit before the food has time to digest in the stomach; for often the cause of the throat lies hidden in the throat and is dislodged by vomiting; or let the patient eat a piece of bread or a leaf of lettuce or a bite of dry bread; or take a piece of dry sea sponge, soak it in vinegar, and then swallow it, for when it reaches the place where the thorns are stuck, they will be dislodged. Or take an eel and dip it in vinegar, and let it lie there until it is soft, then swallow it, for it will be driven into the place where the thorns are stuck, and they will come out; or take a needle and push it in and pull it out.
But if they are not dislodged by these means, then use a lead instrument shaped like this:
And it should be thicker than a little finger, and at its end there should be a cavity which you insert into the patient's throat with ease.
And let the patient tilt his head back, and be careful not to touch his throat bones, so that he may pull on it or press on the bone or thorn with his hand, or that the doctor do so with his hand.
But the patient himself should do this, for he knows best where the cause is located and can press it down from above while pulling up on the instrument, according to the amount by which he is able to relax; then it will be dislodged.
Chapter 39.
On the extraction of a blood clot from the throat.
When there is blood clotting after we have described the treatment with remedies and they do not work, then consider the throat of the patient on the upper surface, for you must examine his tongue with an instrument which we have recommended.
So if you see the blood clot, remove it with a small needle or with a thin, decently pointed instrument.
And if you cannot remove it with that, then take a hollow, curved tube and insert it into the patient's throat; then place a red-hot iron in the cavity of the tube, and do this as many times as necessary (until the blood clot is dead and comes out of the throat), and the patient abstains from water all day.
And then take a sponge soaked in warm water, and wipe the patient' mouth with it; and do not drink anything else for an hour or more, wiping his mouth with the sponge every now and then, for as soon as he feels the water, he will spit out the blood clot.
But if it is not dislodged by what we have recommended, then smoke the patient' mouth with camphor or asafetida through the instrument which we have recommended for smoking the uvula.
Do this, according to how bad it is.
And there is another way of smoking it: take a bowl in which are burning coals and the bowl is covered with a cloth, and in the middle of the cloth there is a hole, and place the end of the instrument in that hole; then smoke the patient; let the patient tilt his head back so that the smoke reaches the blood clot, for when he feels the smoke, the blood clot will come out.
And if it does not work, then repeat the smoking many times; and let the patient abstain from drinking, and eat salt and vinegar, and do not drink water, and with this regime it will be dislodged.
And this is the shape of the instrument with which blood clots are extracted from the throat when they are seen; and it is similar to forceps except that it has some curvature: which is inserted into the throat; its end is similar to a stork's beak, which is hooked, and on it there is an aperture, so that when we press down on any object, it does not slip.
Chapter 40.
Here is the sum of the discourse on the diagnosis and section of abscesses.
Abscesses are of many kinds, according to what we remember of them, of each one in this book.
And they differ in their piercing and sectioning by two means: one is for abscesses in themselves; and the other is for those caused by moistness.
And the second way is according to the places in which they occur: for an abscess in the head is different from an abscess in the buttock; and an abscess in a fleshy place is different from an abscess in a joint; and each of them is treated differently by sectioning.
And there are some abscesses which need not be pierced, but only mature with poultices on them or their complement.
And other abscesses are those which are not punctured unless they are mature with poultices on them; and if they are near a joint, the flesh around it is prolonged as the pus is discharged from it, and it causes a contraction of that member, or it is near an important member, and if you delay piercing it until it is mature, then it will affect the main member; or it is near the buttock, so do not pierce it unless it is mature; or it is near the anus, so do not pierce it unless it is completed, lest it affects the parts within the anus, or it is made in the end of it that it is not healed. But know that you know the time of the puncturing of the pustule, and also when it is mature.
And know that it has matured when there is a decrease in pain and fever, and also a decrease in redness and pulse, and the tip of the pustule becomes blunt, and other signs appear.
And know that the puncturing should take place in the most lower part of the pustule, and also when pus comes out from the healing of the eminence.
And the puncturing should always be done lengthwise along the flesh or body, if the pustules are on the hands or feet, and in places of the joints, of the tendons, of the nerves, of the veins; and, lastly, in all places alike, in which there is no reflex; for in those where there is a reflex, use puncturing according to that member.
But when the pustule is in a fleshy place, it is better to let the puncturing be done after the digestion of it is confirmed, as we have said; for if you puncture it before that, the body of it is prolonged, and much filth comes out, and its lips become hard and deep.
But some pustules are punctured according to the breadth of the flesh or body, as need requires, or according to that member which feels pain.
And you shall give a small puncturing in the great pustules, and a large and ample puncturing or many small ones according to the diversity of the sizes of the pustules.
And others are of pustules in which the cord is hollow and cut, when it is made thus that bread and is made in a term that it was already, as with that which happens in trots of dublec and of buboes.
And of those are in which it is cut with three angles; and of those is in which it is cut thus as the shape of a leaf of myrtle, as well as the pustules of the armpits.
And of them are in which round incisions and lunar incisions are administered, and resembling those.
But to him to whom it is not thus with his pustules, superficial or flat incisions are made only to the superficial ones.
And when the pustule is large and has already collected much pus, you shall puncture it and not be afraid to extract all of its pus in that hour; have extracted a part of it, and then close up the pustule until the next day, and then extract a larger part, and do this several times according as there is a discharge.
And especially if the patient is of a cold nature, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old man in decrepitude, for the animal spirit is many times dissolved by the discharge of pus, and the patient dies soon after, and you operate on them.
So keep this chapter with great caution, and then your puncturing in which you puncture these pustules, wash the wounds and consider therefore if the wound of the pustule is small, or a flat section, then you shall administer the which of oil or of old vinegar; and if the pustule is large, and the fissures of the puncturing are many, then you shall pause with your fingers in each crack until they come together.
And if in the pustule a part of the cord is cut off or you have hollowed it around its circuit, then you shall complete it with old vinegar or with thread made of linen cloth, thus as when you treat boils or ulcers, without moisture; and strengthen it on the third day; and then process it and cure it with that which you use for ointments until it is healed.
But if there is a flow of blood in the hour of your operation, then you shall administer water and vinegar rubbed together with a linen cloth, and place that on the place of the flow of blood several times.
But if the flow of blood persists, then you shall administer medicine and cure it with powders which I have recommended in many places of this our book and division.
But if it is in the winter time, and the place of the pustule is a place of many nerves, then you shall pour powder into vinegar and hot oil, and place that on the places.
And if it is in the summer, and the places are fleshy, then you shall place powdered herbs moistened with water and oil or vinegar and oil, and do this every third day as we have said, and then open up the pustule and wash it and administer to its cure that which is convenient to it until it is healed.
And thus is what is necessary of the knowledge of the cure of pustules universally, but according to the way of distinction I have already said of each pustule in what manner is the way of its cure specifically.
Chapter 41.
Of incisions of pustules which come in the cord of the head.
In the cord of the head are small pustules, and they are of species of knots which contain membranes that are made to them; and the species of them are many.
And from them are bumps, and from those is contained moisture resembling lime. And from those are which contain moisture resembling powder, and resembling them; and from those are which are scaly, hard.
And in the section of all of them, and in the extraction of those there is no fear, as you must extract them it does not contradict the artery.
And the operation in the section of those is that you express those with an instrument the form of which see below, the one which is called entromes, knowing that it contains.
For if what it contains is moisture, then split that one with an incision according to its length by a superficial incision according to this form:
And begin in the incision of line .B to line .G. So when the moisture is discharged, then you scrape that one by which it contains that moisture, and let there be no cause of any, for repeated incisions return if there is any cause from that one.
And then immerse vinegar in Egyptian ointment, if it is present, and if not, in water and salt; and fill that with that the wound and let that stay until another day, for by that you corrode all that is broken of that membrane.
And then apply ointment to that one again secondly and thirdly if it needs it, knowing that you are confident that there is no cause of that membrane; then cure the wound with ointment until it is healed.
And if the pustule contains a knotted vein, then you shall cut that one according to this form: By incision having the shape of a cross, and cut hooks between two lips of the incision and scrape that one throughout its length, and apply your strength in extracting the membrane which contains that.
But if your artery opposes you, then do that which I will tell you first.
And similarly do in the pustule suppuration of incision and cure as we have said; and incision on suppurating pustule is less bloody, for it is of little blood and little moisture.
And some times some of these pustules are in the head in some people with whom there is no moisture; the cause of which is that they have hit upon one in the head of an old woman and rubbed the pustule thus with a hard, rough, white pebble, which could not be touched, and if it hit any person, it would blister.
But for the other abscesses in the head or elsewhere that are not included in this chapter, as well as the abscesses that occur on the heads of children and from the roots of the ears, the incision of all these should be superficial.
And make the incision in those with the lower part of the pus so that it drains the body of the pus to the lower parts.
Then treat those with what is convenient for their healing.
Chapter 42.
Of the incision of scrofula which happens in the neck.
These abscesses often appear on the neck, armpits, and groins; sometimes they occur in other parts of the body as well.
And some are generated among them, and all scrofula of these is within their own membrane, as well as in the nodes and abscesses of the head, as we have described earlier.
And the kinds of these scrofula are various: some are stony, and some contain humidity, and some are malignant and do not respond to treatment.
Therefore, when you see one of good disposition in the Touchment, whose color of what is manifest is close to the color of the cord, and is swollen all over, and is not attached to the nerves of the neck, or to the veins, or to the artery, and is not deep, you should investigate that with a superficial cut from above the line of 30 degrees to below the body of the line of 24 degrees, and score it from all sides, and stretch out its lips with a hook, or with several hooks if you have need of them, as we have said in the abscesses of the head, and extract it little by little.
And it is more careful that the vein or nerve not be cut.
And be careful that the spatula not be very sharp so that it does not accidentally touch you with the incision or disturb the patient, and make an incision only where it is necessary to do so; for if you cut a vein or artery and forbid yourself from your operation, then stop the bleeding with vitriol triphate or other powders which stop blood flow, and close up the wound, and leave that which rests beneath the keenness of the abscess and let the wound be softened and begin to discharge pus. When the blood is abstained.
Therefore, return to your operation until you have completed it.
And then inquire with your finger if there is any cause of the other small scrofula; therefore, cut into those and clean them.
And if there is a great vein in the root of the large scrofula, then you should not cut that scrofula from its root. But before you let it fall by itself without causing harm.
Then fill the wound with old cotton wool which you have already saturated in Egyptian ointment, and then treat it.
And if you have cut the whole scrofula, then you should grasp the two lips of the wound and suck gently until no more superfluity remains.
But if you see that there is superfluity due to the greatness of the scrofula, then understand how to cut its root and drain it and administer the appropriate treatment and what is said.
And that of the scrofula which contain humidity, pierce it with a superficial cut where you see the site of its maturity, and make an incision so that it drains the pus to the lower parts of the body, as we have said.
And then administer a piercing, leeches with ointment and plasters to those, so that it corroses what is left of the corrosion. And then when you see the wound already cleaned, then treat that with generative flesh ointment until it is healed.
Chapter 43.
Of the incision of the boil of an abscess within the gullet.
The ancients wrote about this incision in the pilhot, and we have not seen anyone in our land who has performed it.
And this is the inscription of their language.
But in men who have squintiness, so that the extraction of the pilhot is avoided, lest all the veins and the major nerves of the patient are cut here.
But in those who have abscesses cauterized in the mouth or gullet or two ears, when the malady is not in the cane, use the incision of the pilhot to avoid destruction which is made by piercing.
Therefore, when we want this, let us cut the pilhot below three circles of the circles of the pilhot, or four with a small incision for width in that which is between two circles by quantity, and let the incision be in the diaphragm, not in the cartilage, and this site is appropriate for incision, for it is deprived of flesh and the vessels of blood from it are drawn out.
And if the patient is fearful, then let him stretch out his gullet with a hook, and then split the membrane so that he might reach the canal, but avoid the blood vessels if he sees any cause for doing so.
And then cut the ciplach according to what we have described, and it is significant about the incision of the canal by the flame from which it has issued and by the abstention of voice.
And leave the wound open for a certain time.
Therefore, when the hour is reduced in which the piercing is feared, join together the two lips of the membrane of the wound and cut that only to the cartilage.
And then administer medicines that cause flesh to grow within so that it may be healed.
And Al-Bucasis said that the sum of our speech which we have described is this: some of those abscesses in the gullet of the patient have been cauterized, and the patient has come to death, and his throat is constricted, and some want to cut the epiglottis so that the patient might breathe over the site of the wound by any respiration, and he is saved from death.
And therefore they commanded to leave the wound open until the malady of the malady is consumed: and its malady lasts for three days, and then they commanded to close the wound, and treat it until it is healed.
And what I have seen by my eyes is that one woman served a man and cut him in the gullet and made an incision on it of the pipe of the lung, and he was called to his cure, and when he opened the mouth, blood flowed from the wound just as it did from the dead, and he uncovered the wound and drew out the blood which was flowing from the wound.
Therefore, he confessed that she had not cut a vein or artery, and the wind came out from the wound, and he treated it until it was healed with fire.
And he did not accuse the servant unless he had raged in the throat, and then some days later he returned to his sickness of his own disposition.
Now he says that there is no fear in the incision of the pilhot.
Chapter 44.
Of the incision upon an abscess which occurs in the gullet outward, and is called a hernia of the gullet.
This hernia of the gullet is a great abscess according to the color of the body, and it occurs in women.
And it occurs in two ways, for it is either natural or accidental.
And in nature there is no cure for it.
And the accidental is according to two methods, of which one is like fatty nodes, and the other method is like an abscess, which is caused by a knot in an artery, and in both there is pain. And do not place pressure on him with a needle except in the case of one that is small. And you should examine him and investigate him as I have told you, and if you find it to be like a fatty node, and it is not suspended by any of the veins, then you should cut into that just as you would with nodes, and remove that along with what contains it from the skin and bursa; but if not, then you should probe throughout his body, and then treat the area with something that will promote healing until he is healed.
Chapter 45.
Of the section of the species of nodes.
There are many species of nodes, and I have already described all of their species in the division.
And one should also count the difference between a node and an abscess as causing doubt.
Therefore I say that with an abscess there is heat and violent pain until the ebullition of the superfluous matter is relieved; and it is complete putrefaction when the fever, pain, and heat cease.
But with a node there is no heat or fever or pain; instead it contains the lion's tooth which is in its own sack.
And it is according to the color of the body, and its beginning is with a lump and it is made in this way with vacua, either greater or smaller, and they are according to two species, for some are fatty and contain moisture, and the colors of moisture are many, as I described in the division.
Therefore, when you come to the cure of a node, probe it and pierce it at its beginning with an instrument called a probe, according to its form as it will appear in the chapter which is next.
And it is the manner of inquiry into abscesses and all nodes; take this instrument and insert it into the most moist part which you find in the abscess, and twist your fingers with it little by little until you know that the instrument has penetrated the membrane.
Then finish with your hand according to the measurement of the size of the abscess; then withdraw the probe and consider what has come out in its track.
And if the moisture runs out, of whatever color it may be, then you should cut into it superficially as I have said in the other abscesses.
And if no moisture comes out from around the probe, then know that it is fatty.
And dry it with superficial incisions in the shape of a cross according to this form: thus with what you have been taught; suspend that with pins, and scrape the membrane away from all parts with ease, and guard the skin or sack, if possible, over it, and withdraw that pus along with the node.
But if it is ruptured in the operation, it is not possible to withdraw that pus; instead do so at intervals so that no cause remains behind.
For if any cause remains behind, little or much, the node will return according to the most.
And if you see that some small part remains behind, then complete the wound with some powdered corrosive drugs, and bind the wound tightly, and place something hot over the abscess, and cure it by another method until it is healed.
And if it is a large node, then cut both lips of it and cure that with what it was incarnated.
But if it comes with a pulsating vein, or not-pulsating, then you should cut and fill the area around it with powdered vitriol, and let that rest for two or three days until the swelling of the blood subsides; then return to cutting what is ruptured of the node.

Chapter 47.
Of the cure of men's breasts, which are similar to those of women.
Sometimes the breasts of some men become enlarged due to a change in sleep habits when they start to grow hair, and then their breasts become swollen, resembling those of women, and they become roman-like.
And when you examine that, cut it with a lunar incision from line B to line G, and then completely remove the growth, fill the wound with medicated plaster, sew together the two lips of the wound, and heal the patient.
But if the breast sags towards the sides and becomes soft like a woman's due to its size, then cut it in two along its sides with two lunar-shaped incisions, so that each half contains the other, as the longer line contains the shorter one, from line B to line G. Then remove the cord between the two lips of the wound, cut out the fat, and administer what we have said about sewing and powders, which are necessary in the cure, until it is healed.
And if you do not complete the incision of that which must be cut for the restlessness of the patient and the flow of blood, then fill the wound with cotton soaked in corrosive ointment and leave it until it corrodes what is rotten inside, and then cure the patient until he is healed.
Chapter 48.
Of piercing abscesses that come from below with itching.
Those abscesses that come from below with itching are of the species of scrofula, hard, and they contain a bag full of pus.
And some contain moisture; and those that contain moisture should be cut with a lunar incision from line G to line B. And when all the pus is evacuated from the abscess of the scrofula, then fill it with old ointment and leave it for another day.
And then the ointment should be applied and the wound should be cured with a suitable ointment until it is healed.
And if the abscess of the species of nodules and scrofula is, then cut it as we have said in the section on scrofula.
But if the wound is spread so that it causes pus, then administer cauterization on it as we have said before.
Chapter 49.
Of incisions of abscesses that happen through an artery or vein.
When an artery is broken and the vein is collapsed above it, then many times there is an abscess that happens through an artery or vein: when an abscess happens through an artery, it is long drawn out into the depth of the body; and when you push on the abscess with your fingers, you feel a sound in it that indicates stridor.
And when it happens through a vein, it is round to the surface of the body.
And incision on this abscess is dangerous and especially in that which is below the armpits, and in the groin, and in the neck, and in many parts of the body; and it is large, therefore its cure by cautery should be avoided, and especially in that which is at the extremities, or to the head, it should be avoided.
But if it is due to inflammation of the orifice of the artery, cut an incision in the vein along its length; and then open the incision with pincers and the artery, and loosen the tunics so that they are uncovered.
And then put an awl on it and make it penetrate to the other side, and tighten the artery with a double-fold ligature in two places, which will cause you to push it out from both temples.
And then plug up the hole between two ligaments with a spatula so that all the blood in it is stopped, and the abscess will be dissolved.
And then administer cure in which pus is engendered within so that the ligaments fall down; and then cure it with suitable ointments until it is healed.
And if it is an abscess through an incision of a vein, then you should hold with your hand what is possible for the abscess over the vein, and then insert the awl below where you have held with your hand, and make it penetrate; and there will be a double ligature within so that you draw out from the other side, and then tie the abscess with a strong ligature according to what we have said to you in the ligature of two parts with two ends.
But if you fear that drawing out the ligature, then insert the needle below all of the abscess after the incision of the first needle, and tighten your fingers in four places.
Then dry up the abscess in its middle part where it has risen so that what is in it is pushed out, and then insert the superfluity of the vein, and leave what is inside it.
And then place on it powder which you have soaked in wine and oil, and then administer the cure that is made with cauterizations and ointments until it is healed.
Chapter 50 of the abscess which happens through torture of nerves.
As it happens in an artery and vein, and similarly, an abscess happens in nerves when they happen in their compression or happen through a superfluous strike, and similarly.
And it is done to them in the places of the joints or in the talons, or in any place where the joints are crushed.
And it is a severe pustule, and is similar in color to the rest of the body, and there are six of them on his body, and when they are pressed with force, the patient seems stunned.
And the pustule is not located in the chest area, but below the neck, and he is painful all over his body, and does not want to move forward or backward.
Therefore, for those who have the pustules in their joints, it is not necessary to use a cautery of iron, since they will soon recover on their own.
However, if the pustule is on the head or forehead and affecting the eyes, treat it with spathum. But if there are few pustules, then cut them out with forceps at their roots.
And if it is large, then open it with a scalpel, and clean out the wound; and stop the bleeding with a tourniquet, and stitch up the wound; and dress the wound so that it may heal.
Chapter 11.
Of the section of a pustule which happens to the jaw, which happens in the belly.
It happens to some people that they get spots on their bellies and other parts of the body, which are called warts due to their resemblance to mushrooms, whose roots are subtle but whose tops are thick; and indeed the lips of these people become withered, and it is found in those who are small, and also in those who are greatly magnified.
And I have seen one like this, and on his belly were two things which were most similar to mushrooms, and there was no difference between them and white ones, except that their roots were thinner.
And indeed the lips of these people were withered and cracked, and moisture flowed from them all the time.
Therefore I cut into one of them and found in its inside a stone weighing 15 ounces. And the other one weighed 6 ounces.
And when you cut into it, consider whether the patient is humid or dry, and if the color of the stone is white, humid, and of thin roots, then open it with a broad scalpel, and let it be cauterized in the fire, because much blood will flow from the wound; and if the blood flows, cauterize it.
And if you see the patient is fearful and frightened, be cautious about cutting with iron; but instead take fresh lead ore, and apply it to the stone in the manner we have described; and let that sit for two days.
And then tighten it in the grip of the lead wire; therefore do not cease to press down on the large lump until it is cut off and falls away by itself.
But if the stone has thick roots, then in the cutting of it there is a cause for fear and dread, especially in that which is in the belly.
But it is possible that you can cut only half of it, and then cauterize it so that it does not return.
And then dress the wound so that it may heal.
And beware of cutting a stone which is of dusky color, of little feeling, and with little regard to the body, because that one is full of cancer.
And I will bring up the memory of a certain cranium.
Chapter 12.
Of the treatment of protrusion of the navel.
Protrusion of the navel is caused by many things; or by fissures of the diaphragm which is above the belly, and from it the membrane or intestine, depending on where the other ruptures are; or by blood which flows from a vein or artery according to what is before us, or by constriction of the intestines within it.
But if it is by a fissure of the diaphragm and loosening of the membrane, then the color of the pustule is similar to that of the body; and there is little pain with it, and indeed it appears in various places. And if it is by protrusion of the intestine, then its appearance will be as we have described, with more violent variation, and when you press it with your fingers, it hides itself, and then returns; and soon it is found again, and is greatly magnified due to bathing and violent exertion.
But if it is by moisture, then there is little pain and it does not hide when you press it with your hand, nor is it constricted or crushed.
And if it is by blood, then there appear with these signs the pustule inclining towards blackness.
But if it is by dry flesh, then it is a severe pustule, large and hard, and is fixed according to its amount.
But if it is by intestinal protrusion, then there is little pain when touched.
And in its treatment, you should consider whether the protrusion of the navel is by blood from an artery or vein, or by intestinal protrusion; therefore it behoves you to abstain from treating it, because there is fear and dread in that one as we have taught in the chapter where we spoke about pustules from an artery and a vein.
And if the protrusion of the navel is by the intestine or membrane, then have the patient lean back and stand extended; and indeed touch with your fingers around the entire navel, and indeed command him to stand facing you with his chest against your chest, and indeed circle with a broad scalpel around the navel over the area which you have touched with your fingers; and indeed extend the pustule towards the upper parts with a large needle; and indeed ligate around it with strong thread or with twine in a decent manner.
And then open the middle of the extended pustule over its ligament and put your finger inside that hole and probe the intestine; and if you have blocked it or restrained it by the ligament, then indeed withdraw your fingers and push the intestine towards the interior parts of the belly.
And if you have blocked the membrane, then take it with a needle; and cut off the superfluities of it.
But if it is opposite your artery or vein, then surround it a lot, and then return to your operation; and take two needles and put them in those two strong threads and put the two needles around the pustule in the form of crosses, the which you make to penetrate; and then tighten the pustule into four parts over the needles.
And if you want, remove the needles and let the extended flesh return to its position and fall by itself; or cut into it when it is thinned out and probed, and then dress that with what we have spoken of as a poultice onto the wound until it is healed.
And if the protrusion of the navel is by dry flesh in it or by moisture, then indeed you should suck out the pustule as we have said and draw out the blood or moisture which you block in it, and then dress that with what covers it so that it consolidates the wound.
Chapter 13.
Of the treatment of a cranium.
We have already said in the division of a cranium and how it is the way to its cure by medicines, and that it is cut off in it the cure by iron so that it is not ulcerated; and we have spoken of a cranium engendered in the mother and cautery of its cure.
And the ancients say that some times a cranium is found in a place where its eradication is possible, like a cranium which is on the chest or the buttock and similar to the members assigned to extract all of it, especially when it starts small.
But when it is old and severe, do not approach the patient, for I have not seen anyone heal from that illness nor do I know of anyone who has recovered from it.
And the operation on him is that you proceed and let the patient bleed and purge black bile several times, and then cut into him, if there is found a full, manifest hernia.
Then prepare the patient with preparation in which he is placed for operation, and then pierce the wound with nails that suit it; and then hollow out from all parts with a good saw, thorough examination within so that no cause of the disease remains. And let the blood flow, and do not bandage it loosely, and press out the places, and wipe off the thick blood with your hand or with an instrument that is suitable to you among your instruments.
But if the flow of thick blood from a vein or artery gives you trouble, then cauterize that inside so that the flow of blood is stopped, and then treat it with another treatment until it is healed.
Chapter 44
Of treatment for dropsy.
We have already recommended in the division of the species of dropsy with water, and the characteristics of each species, of its treatment with medicines.
And that which is cured with iron is only the species of altithas alone, and it must not be approached with iron to the species of tympany nor to the species of hyparka, because it is deadly.
And when you have treated this species of tympany with medicines and it does not respond to your treatment, then consider, because if the patient already has debility, or has another disease such as another dropsy, like one in which there is cough or chest or abdominal pain and similar diseases, then beware that you do not treat them with iron, for fear of that.
But if you see the patient in robust health, and with no other disease but dropsy alone, and not a child or old man, then the manner of operation on him is that you elevate the patient between your hands, and then press his abdomen with your hand, filling the water to the bottom of the navel, and then take thorny ash wood according to this form:
let it be of two pointed parts long, with a pointed end like ash wood; but let there be in it some small brevity from time to time, so that in the operation with it you do not pass into the intestines, and let him drink that.
And then consider if the generation of dropsy is from part of the intestines, because then you must with section elongate the navel from the bottom, in the right of him over the navel.
But if the generation of dropsy is from disease of the liver, then your section must be on the left of the navel by three fingers.
And if its generation is from melasma, then your section should be on the right.
And do not let your section be over the side where the patient wants to lie so that the superfluities do not flow to that place.
Then pierce with the instrument throughout the cavity, and insert into that section, and elevate your hand with the ash wood between the cavity and the pharynx, and drain him; and if it is the quantity of a nail or more.
Then pierce the pharynx so that the ash wood reaches the desired location, and it is where the water is. Then withdraw him and insert an instrument of which this is the form: and it is like a tube of silver or gold or lead, to which in the lower end there is a small hole, and on its sides are three holes: two from one side and one from the other side; and its end is beveled according to the manner of a feather, as follows:
And at the upper end of it there is a ring, because when the instrument reaches the water, then that immediately withdraws over the instrument, therefore evacuates from the water in the middle quantity, for if you evacuate from that more than it should not in the hour, then the patient dies from resolution of his animal spirit, or he suffers five pains which are approaching death.
But it evacuates from that according to the quantity of his strength and according to what you see are the dispositions of the patient's strength, from his pulse and his goodness.
Then withdraw the instrument and tie up the water which causes it because as soon as it is tied by the cavity, then the hole that is over the pharynx from which you have pierced that according to that manner.
Then return the instrument on another day if he can tolerate it, and withdraw a little water, and do this for several days out of fear, and beware of error so that it does not return to the water except for a little.
But if you fear for the patient and let out of the water a large quantity, then treat him with dry medicines so that he is healed.
And cauterize over the stomach, and the melasma and the liver, and also the extraction of the water according to what I have recounted in that which precedes.
Chapter 45
Of the treatment for children who are born with holes not punctured in their urine places.
Sometimes some of the infants are born from their mother's womb and the tip of their genitals is not punctured (or is tightly drawn or is not in its place).
Then it must be treated with piercing of it as soon as he is born with a very subtle pointed instrument according to this form:
Then insert into the hole a thin nail of lead and ligature it, and leave it for three days or for 4 days.
And when he wants to urinate, let him be urged and urinate; then return that.

Chapter 62.
On incision for inguinal hernia.
Inguinal hernia is nothing but a collection of moisture within the white membrane that lies beneath the muscles of the abdomen and is called the fascia.
And sometimes it occurs in the lower part of the abdominal membrane, where nature has prepared it for the separation of another abdomen; and it is the membrane between the white fascia which we have mentioned earlier, and it is not anything else but fat.
And the cause of this hernia is due to weakness that occurs in the muscles, because through them this material is poured out, and sometimes it occurs due to a blow made to the muscles.
And this moisture has many colors; the color of it inclines towards yellow or blood-red, or red, or is black and slimy, or is water white, and that is what happens most often.
And the signs by which one can tell where this collection of water occurs are these: for if it is in the white fascia which we have mentioned, then the swelling is round and declining a little towards length like the shape of an abdomen, and it appears on the muscle, because the moisture covers that entire part.
And if the moisture is in the lower membrane, then the swelling is round with a separation at the abdomen, and because of this one believes it to be another abdomen.
And if the moisture is between the membrane of the muscles and the white fascia, then it has a flat appearance.
And when you want to know the color of the moisture, then you should probe the color of the moisture in the swelling by inserting a thread into which the shape of the swelling is preceded; and according to what comes out on the thread, judge what is inside it.

Then administer wool soaked in oil and place it on the wound; and administer the stitch which we have recommended  (and in many times the white membrane is cauterized, which we have said near the incision of it they fear a flow of blood, because sometimes this happens) and leave the stitch so that by itself it falls.
But if the healing of it is delayed, then let it be anointed with oil and place that over it so that it falls according to what we have said.
Then cure the wound with the other cure of wounds, so that it is healed.
Chapter 66.
Of a wind hernia.
In this hernia, I have not seen anyone who has been healed on the cure of it with iron.
And the first said that it is done thus as we have recommended in the hernia that is with wine; which is that you sew the vessels near the incision on it with ease of it; and then dry up in the middle place around the abscess with what opened it, so that the vessels fall.
And cure the wound according to what we have said so that it is healed.
Chapter 67.
Of the rupture which is done in the testicles.
Sometimes a rupture in the testicles as we have said, and the site emerges.
And do not let any cause of intestines occur to the testes; and if it does occur, that is few; and return back in all hours.
But if the time with that is prolonged, then a fissure is adjusted in the membrane through which the intestine descends into the membrane; and that happens due to the extension of the membrane of the testicles as we have said, which cause is because the membrane is stretched, and then it becomes soft and the site is abscessed and emerges.
And the cure of it is with cautery as it is preceded by the narration of it.
And in some times it is cured with iron thus: and the patient lies on his back between your hands, and then dry up the site of the rupture of the abscesses that emerge with an incision according to the width of three fingers.
Then strengthen the white membrane which is below the skin so that it is exposed.
Then take the rod and place it over the prominent site of the membrane, and press it against the bone of the belly.
Then press the two prominent sites on the end of the rod of the membrane and adjust with the suture one of those to the other.
Then pull out the end of the rod and do not pierce the membrane at all, nor extend the intestine, nor any other cause as you have come to know in the cure of intestinal hernia.
Then cure that with the cure of wounds, and as you pierce the threads, cleanse that and restore the wound so that it is consolidated; because the membrane is contracted and the prominence of the rupture is not adjusted.
And cautery is better in this site because it is closer to health.
Chapter 68.
Of the softening of the skin of the testicles.
Many times the skin of the testicles in some men is softened because the flesh which is between that is softened, and it is attributed to the guard of it.
Therefore it is necessary for that one who is asked in the cure of it to make the patient lie on his back according to his back, and to put all the skin which is softened onto the natural skin; and then adjust two lips with a stitch.
And if you want, cut in the beginning the superfluity of the softened skin with three or four incisions and with a firm stitch.
Then pierce between the stitches; and then cure by the cure of the other wounds so that it is healed and the threads fall.
Chapter 69.
Of castration.
Know that castration in our law is excommunicated, but for the cause it is allowed to me that I remind you of it in this book; and it is not necessary to remind it unless by two ways, of which one is so that it is in the science of the doctor when he is questioned about it, so that he knows its cure if it happens; and the other way is that we many times have need of castration of other beasts for our youths by them, as with horses, oxen, pigs, and similar to beasts.
And therefore I say that castration is done in two ways: or by incising, or by piercing with an incision.
But in that which is done by incising, the path of the operation is to let the beast bleed in water so that its testes are softened and hang down. Then take those with your hand so that they are resolved and do not appear below the touch.
But in castration which is done by piercing and incision, keep the beast and press the skin of its testicles with your left hand.
Then tie the suspensory, and pierce above each wound by an incision so that two wounds are made.
Then pierce those which you will have healed after they are healed. And do not apply anything over the head of those with a headache, but rather use a subtle compress on the temples.
And this method of castration is better, which is done by strangulation, for strong strangulation will leave no cause in the testes that the beast desires coitus.
Then treat the wound until it is healed.
Chapter 70:
Of the cure for hermaphroditism.
Hermaphroditism in men occurs in two ways: the first is where there appears a swelling in the space between the testes, in that which is between two testes, a figure like a woman's vulva.
And sometimes urine flows from it, located in the scrotum of the testes.
But in women it is of one kind, and that is that the clitoris on top of the vulva resembles two testes of a man, slightly swollen at the entrance like a foreskin, and has two testes.
And the cure is of three kinds: two from men and one from women. And it is that you should insert those tightly packed tissues until the moisture of that thing escapes, and then cure those with the cure for other wounds.
And in the second kind of men where urine flows from it and it is in the scrotum of the testes, there is no cure nor incision for it.
Chapter 21:
Of a hernia and prominent flesh due to causes in women.
A strong hernia is tightly packed over natural causes and is stressed, and sometimes it is magnified in some women to such an extent that it spreads like men, and pervades into sexual intercourse.
So if you have the excess of hernia, hold it with your hand or a bandage and insert.
And do not finish the incision, especially in the vein of the artery, so that it does not cause a flow of blood.
Then cure that with the cure for wounds until it is healed.
But born flesh is flesh that grows in the womb of the mother and fills it up, and often it is protruded to the openings according to the appearance of a tail (and because of this some earlier writers called it "tailed malady"); therefore we should insert as we do with hernia, and cure that until it is healed.
Chapter 72:
Of the cure for anus pain.
Anus pain is when the clitoris of a woman is not pierced or has a small hole. And it is either natural or accidental.
Accidental is due to a malady that has preceded it, and that is caused either by tightly packed flesh or by a subtle swelling or thickness.
And it is caused either in the womb of the mother or her ribs or above them or below them, and it prohibits coitus and pregnancy and menstruation, and often prohibits childbirth as well.
And the knowledge of it is gained by examination by the midwife, if the swelling is apparent, then by prodding; but if it is not apparent, then you approach that with your fingers or with a rod.
But if the swelling is due to a subtle compress and it is protruded between the two labia, then you cut and burst that.
And you pause on both labia with your fingers, and then place your fingers indicating the two hands clenched.
And the woman be on her back with her thighs extended, and then extend both labia with force so that subtle compress is broken and the swelling opened.
And then take wool and soak it in oil and place it over that spot, and keep it wet with a cloth every day so that the cut does not heal up again.
But if the swelling is large and thick, then you should insert that with a spatulum made of wood or a twig of myrrh.
But if the swelling is due to flesh, then suspend it with a bandage and insert that.
And let there be to you the medicines which stop the flow of blood without biting, like aha cataria, and dragon's blood, and onions, tightly bound with white of egg.
And then administer a large leaden cautery so that the wound is not healed superficially.
And keep that for several days and administer heat of lard.
Then it should be cured with the other cure of consolidation until it is healed.
And sometimes it happens in the womb of mothers of others' children, and then you should insert according to this manner. But if it is due to phlegmatic humor, then let the phlegmatic humor not be counteracted by iron in any way.
Chapter 73:
Of the cure for hemorrhoids and of a tail and of red botch which happens in the clitoris of women.
Hemorrhoids are an appearance of orifices of many veins from which blood flows continually from them, and when hemorrhoids are old and they are prolapsed.
And I have already mentioned in the division of those and their signs, and described them as those which received cure and those who did not receive cure.
Therefore I say that hemorrhoids and theyls when they are in the womb of the mother and do not appear with the sense, then in those let there be no cure with iron.
But those which are in the orifices of the mother above all senses, then those should be cured.
And you shall place the woman in a warm bath and then extend it with the fingers or with a rough cloth, and insert those with the nails.
And then sprinkle over that one of the powders which cause blood flow without biting, like a cassia and its likes.
And then pluck her feet for an hour, and then place that in cold water.
And if the flow of blood persists, then let it be cauterized with a caustic made of sumac and grains and thorns and their likes.
And then take bran of wheat and cook that with honey and vinegar and make a plaster with it over her back.
And if the blood is scanty, let it be; but if not, then let it adhere with two leeches, and to the nipples its excision.
And then take wool and soak it with juice of colandro or with juice of arnagloza or with juice of guara viler made with vinegar, and make it adhere to the spot; and then cure the spot with unguents until it is healed.
And then cure that until it is healed.
Chapter 74:
Of accidental piercing in the womb.
Many kinds of hemorrhoids happen in the womb, like phlegmatic humor and ulcerative apostema and suppurative and gangrenous and fistulas and hemorrhoids and others' apostemas. And I have already mentioned these diseases and their kinds and their signs, and their cures in the division.
And let him ask in this treatment of hemorrhoid cauterized which appears in the womb when it is of hemorrhoids that are prolapsed, and if you want to know in what manner its incision is made with iron.
When you consider that the pain of the pustule in its beginning is acute with percussion and phlegm and fever, then see if there is any swelling and feel it, then do not cut into it, but treat it with what aids in maturation until the sharpness of the accidents ceases.
And then you make the woman lie on her side with two pillows; recline on her back and adjust her feet to the lowest part of the belly, let her thighs be spread out, and place her arms below her ears, and tie each one with a bandage as appropriate.
Then the midwife stands on the right side and administers the instrument with which the opening of the womb is made, the shape of which will come in those causes that will be made appropriate.
And when you want to administer this instrument, put the tip of the mother's womb, and what goes into the instrument from the womb should not be more than the width of the mother, and lead the patient. But if the instrument is larger than the width of the womb, then you should put powder on the texture of the width of the womb so that the entry of any instrument into the womb is prohibited.
And you should put the thread that runs through the instrument from the top side, and let the minister have the instrument and turn the thread until the opening of the womb is open.
And when the growth appears and is touched with the hand and is soft and moist, then you should dry the head of it with a broad knife.
And when the pus is evacuated, then you should put in the wound a poultice soaked in rose oil or green oil in which there is some astringency; and place the plaster on the section in the womb.
And place wool over the womb and on the pubic region clean wool soaked in water in which there are crushed mallows.
Then it should be treated for two days with a ointment which is appropriate for that until it is healed.
And sometimes the womb and the plaster are washed with water and honey, and then anointed with water in which there is crushed lily or long aristology, and then return to the ointment.
And if the plaster is inside the swollen womb, then you should be prohibited from treating it with iron, have that treated with what we have said in the division.
Chapter .lxxv.
To teach midwives how the living fetus should be treated when it is born according to an unnatural figure.
It is necessary that the midwife know at the beginning the figure of the natural childbirth by its signs, and it is that when you see the woman express at the lowest parts and desire to smell the air, and about it is above her on top, and hastens the birth of the fetus, then you know that this birth is according to a natural figure, and is its ejection onto its head, and the second with it or suspended or hanging from the umbilical cord.
Therefore when you see those signs, then the belly of it should be compressed so that the fetus descends gently as it descends over its head, and the second with it or suspended or hanging from the umbilical cord, and is cleansed of those superfluities with a good cleansing.
But that which is other than this birth is unnatural and blameworthy, for when the fetus exits over its feet and its body exits before its head and its feet, and its hand or to the foot of it .I., or its head and hand exits or to the belly of it, and strongly turned onto its neck, and resembling the figures of it blameworthy.
It is therefore necessary that the midwife be wise and subtle in all those causes, and that she keep from error and deception.
And I will show you all figures of these, and what craft is in those so that it may be signified by that and be established on that.
When the fetus exits over its head by natural exertion, and that is vigorous on the woman and is a difficult birth for it, and sees the strength of it already weakened, then do that , or let the women hold it, and evaporate the heat of it with fenugreek cooked in water and with moist oils.
Then the midwife inserts between its lips a small knife and splits with it the second with it or dries that with her finger within it until it runs that which is within it of moisture. And press the belly of the woman so that it descends the fetus.
But if it does not descend, then let the woman be anointed with mustard and mustard with chickpeas.
And then command it, the midwife, that she be compressed and make her vomit with spice; and stop the mouth of it and its nose for one hour, for the fetus will come out immediately.
And if both hands of the fetus are out at the beginning, then you should reduce those by little with ease. But if it does not obey the insertion, then place the woman on a pillow and lift its feet up, and then rock the pillow onto the ground; and let the woman be held so that she does not fall due to the rocking.
And if the hands are not bent back and the fetus is lifeless, then insert those and pull out the limb of the fetus or tie the body to the hand of it with a cloth and pull that equally, for it will come out immediately.
When the fetus exits over its feet, then you should push those up and then turn the fetus a little, and then grasp one of its feet and stretch those little by little.
But when it is inside the thighs, then you command it that it be expressed, and make it vomit with spice, for it will come out if God wills.
And if it is not come out with what we have recommended, then you return the fetus little by little as you place that according to a natural figure, for it will come out immediately with gentle ejection.
And if it is prohibited by everything that we have recommended, then take mustard and dissolved gum, and beat them both in the mortar with a good beating, and apply them to the heat of the woman, to the lowest part of the belly of it. Then make her sweat in lukewarm water so that she acquires the phlegm.
And when you see that the lowest parts of it are softened, then do to it fumigation of myrrh and stop that on it. And when you have done the fumigation for one hour, then make it sweat on a pillow, and then let it vomit and open the mouth of it, and lift from that, and press the lowest part of its belly with gentle compression, for the fetus will come out immediately.
Examine the fester lengthwise with one of your fingers. Try to reduce it with your hand, but if you cannot reduce it, then lift the woman and make her walk.
And if she cannot walk, then have her lie on her side, and strike her thighs with a violent concussion, and administer remedies which you have and count from mucilages.
And if childbirth has occurred, then have her lie on her back, and study the reduction of the hand, and open the fester according to its natural shape, and make the woman sneeze and instruct him to compress himself while it is forgotten.
Examine the fester on the neck with your fingers expanded and the fascia of the patient is towards the two of his mother. Have the midwife hold the hand of the fester and gradually roll it, and have that facilitate it.
And when it is open and how much it is, then pause over the navel of the patient what we have recommended of oil and mucilages.
And then instruct him to close his hand gradually, and when you have done that, then have her lie on one side and instruct him to be inclined on the right side, and then instruct him to be compressed; and make her sneeze with an onion. Exit of the fetus prepared on the side.
When they are about to exit from the mother according to this manner, consider, and then you insert your second finger with your nail inside so that it is evacuated of moisture.
And if the fetus is suspended over the face and neck of the patient, then you insert that of the emblic, so that it is not retained and delayed.
And then press the fetus to the insides within while you pause that according to what it covers, and instruct the woman to compress herself several times, and it will exit forgotten with easy exit if God wills it.
Exit of twins or multiple fetuses. Know that twins are born many times, and some give birth to three or four, but that is strange and rare; but their causes are nature, and not life.
And count those, whether they are multiples, a second one, and they are separated by a membrane, distinguish those between the ligament in the navel of each of them. And sometimes they exit forgotten like a single fetus with easy natural exit, and sometimes they exit with unforgettable exit as we have recommended.

And if the midwife does what she does with ease and skill, and delay, and is formed according to the whole shape as it is prepared for birth leading to health.
Reminder of that which is formed in the womb from embryos and abortions.
