However, one must consider whether the palm is already turned towards the belly of the hand; then the patient should place the back of their hand on a table below the extension and reduction. And if the dislocation precedes from the back of the hand, then the position of the hand should be intrinsecally on the table so that the doctor's hand can grasp that imminence of the joint.
And if he returns at once, that is good; but if not, then press on the pustule with your finger until it gives way and let it go, and do not repeat this, or else he will not endure nor be able to bear the reduction after so many days have passed.
But the bone will return to its position according to its tortuosity; and if you observe no cause in the patient, except that his hand is relaxed and cannot grasp anything, then know that the nerves are torn or cut, and there is nothing inside him except that it should be tightened with a cautery near its dislocation, and strengthen it there firmly.
Then when the patient is returned to his former state, apply to him the plaster which we have recommended, and let it remain and be tightened for three days; and then let it be loosened and left off, and the hand exercised.
But if his movement is impeded and some heaviness occurs in him, then loosen that with warm water and with friction several times, while he is being eased.
Chapter 29.
Of the cure for dislocation of the teeth.
The teeth are sometimes completely dislocated.
And when any tooth is dislocated to the back of the hand or to its belly, then press on the tooth and drive out the dislocation of it with your fingernails, while it returns to place.
Then support the head of the tooth and suspend that from the part to which it is dislocated, and leave that for two days.
And then suspend and extend that until it is straightened out in its place on the following day.
And when morning comes, loosen that according to the narrative, and do not cease loosening it during the day and exercising with movement, and do so at night as well; and do this for several days until it is tightened.
And feign that it is dislocated to the belly of the hand, and loosen that to that part, and do with it your first operation until it is healed.
And similarly do with it if it is dislocated to other parts.
Chapter 30.
Of the cure for dislocation of the vertebrae in the back.
When complete dislocation occurs to any of the vertebrae in the back or neck, and several vertebrae are displaced from their places, then in that there is no cure, for death awaits the patient.
And a sign of this is that the excretion of the patient is outside his control, and he cannot retain it; and often several members of his body or both legs or both arms, or one of those are relaxed; or one vertebra is displaced from its place, for often it is displaced and often the removal of those to four parts occurs.
Then when that is displaced to the back parts, it is called dislocation of the spine.
But its cure is that you should consider if the dislocation occurred in childhood, for then there is no cure for that, and there is no healing of it at all.
But of that which occurs due to impact or concussion or similarly, the Ancients have spoken of methods of cure with prolix speech, of which the best returns with profit; but I have abridged that which the few excuse from its excess due to my proximity to the intention and its exposition, and in which I have expounded and formed it from diverse instruments, by which I will demonstrate and explain.
And of those, only that which occurs in the back properly is healed by me.
And let the patient be extended on his face over a soft bed, and let him be extended below by an instrument moistened in order that his feet not be bound.
And then a straight staff should be placed, fixed in the earth at the end of the bed around his head, and another staff in air holding up his feet at the other end of the bed.
And one minister should hold the staff and not be fixed in a hole; and another minister should hold the other according to that form.
And then wrap around the head of the patient and let them lift up with their hands the end of the staff which is beneath his head, and extend the other end of the staff to the other staff which is beneath his feet; and then tighten all the cords and do this to the other staff which is beneath his feet.
And then the ministers each extend the cords to the end of the staff, and let the staffs not be displaced from their places where they are fixed, but rather let them be tightened as I have said.
And the doctor should place his palms over the vertebra with strength until it returns to its position, or he should place it on a table and then tighten his feet over the table until it returns.
But if it does not return by this means, then take a table whose breadth or length is in air about three arms, and hollow out in the wall of which we have said that it is near the patient a place into which the end of the table falls. And then place the middle of the table over the vertebra, and the doctor should place his feet over the other end, and tighten well until the vertebra is tightened and returns to its position.
And if you wish, open with a pulley which is turned by hand; and fix in the earth behind the head of the patient two staffs, the length of which are an arm each, and fix the head of him in the end of the pulley two staffs, and let the length be between each staff one palm, and each be fixed in the earth so that it is not displaced.
And there should be a round staff in which is the pulley, and it should be turned in the two holes of the two staffs.
And at its end is a hole in which the staff is formed, the length of which is one palm by that which is turned; and likewise in the two other staffs is similarly.
And then tighten the cords which you have tightened around the feet of the patient in the pulley which is beneath his head, and the cords which you have tightened around his thighs in the turn which is beneath his feet.
And then each pulley should have a minister who turns the pulley with his hand, and the doctor should warm the vertebra as we have said.
And when the vertebra is returned and the place warmed, then consider that you pause on the dislocation a plaster dried with oil of roses, and then pitch; and then pause over the plaster a table whose breadth is three digits or more, and its length should take up the distance of the dislocation, and over the part of the vertebra.
And then let him be tied with a bandage as we have said before, and feed the patient with subtle food until he is healed.
And if there is any swelling in the affected area at the end of the healing process, then medicines that soften and loosen should be administered through oral intake over a long period of time, as we have described; and a lead plate has already been applied to that area.
And sometimes swelling occurs at the base of the spine, and it is caused by that displacement; and there is a bone in that area which should not be subjected to this medicine, because if it is, it will likely cause death.
Chapter 31.
On the treatment of a dislocated hip.
Know that the joint of the hip and the joint of the muscle are not designed to be dislocated, but only to move slightly with a small cavity.
And the joint of the hip is dislocated in four ways: it is dislocated on the inside or outside, or forward or backward.
Most often, it is dislocated to the inside, and less often to the front or back.
And the sign of dislocation to the inside is that when you straighten the leg of the patient, it is longer and more prominent than the healthy one, and the patient cannot bend their foot backward, and there is a swelling on top of the hip joint, because the head of the femur has shifted here.
And the sign of dislocation to the outside is that its features are opposite to the previous description.
And the sign of dislocation forward is that they can only extend their leg, but not bend it at the knee due to pain; if they try to walk on the ball of their foot, they cannot; and their urine is retained, and there is swelling in the groin area, and they walk on their heels.
And the sign of dislocation backward is that they cannot extend or bend their leg at the knee; the leg is shorter than the other, and the groin area is softened, and the head of the femur has shifted backward.
However, the reduction of this dislocation is that you must consider whether the dislocation is old and chronic: if it has been like that for a long time and you administer reduction according to its condition, then it will not be cured completely; and in that case, there should be no prosomecio.
But with the patient who has a recent dislocation, and it is one of the four types of dislocation, then you must try to return the joint to its proper position and extend it toward the inside and outside, and move it to the right and left, for it will quickly return to its place and will not require any other treatment.
But if it does not return to its proper position in this way, then you must prepare a strong bandage and extend the leg of the patient from the lowest part, or with their own hands, or with a bandage tied around the leg above the knee; and another person should hold the end of the bandage while someone else pulls it down below the patient's fingers; then tightly bind the lion's tongue around the head of the femur.
And the extension should be from the inside to the groin, or from the back to the shoulder blade.
And they should all be extended at the same time while the patient is raised from the ground and their leg hangs down.
And this type of extension is common to all four types.
So if the dislocation returns according to what we have said, it is good; but if not, then it is necessary to use any method that one knows of their own cure.
In the proper reduction of it, when it is dislocated to the inside, the patient should lie on their side; then place the bandages over the head of the femur in that area between the head of the femur and the groin; and extend the bandage from above the groin toward the highest part of the collarbone.
And another assistant should hold the patient' leg firmly, press on the large part of the hip joint and extend toward the outside with strong extension, for it will return to its place.
And this is the quickest cure by which this member is reduced compared to the other methods.
But if it is resisted and does not obey the treatment with this method of cure for both feet at the same time, then both feet should be bound together tightly, on the soles and over the instep.
And the length of each band should be the amount of four fingers, and the leg of the patient should be extended more than the other by the amount of two fingers.
And the patient should be suspended over the head of the pillar, and it should be in the middle; and its length from the ground should be the amount of two yards.
And order a strong young man to push down on the head of the femur, and another strong young man should suspend the patient, and the other young man should push up on the hip with strength, for the joint will return to its place quickly.
But in the proper reduction, when it is dislocated to the outside, the patient should lie on their back according to what we have recommended regarding frozen gel; and the bandage should be tightly bound around the leg of the patient and over the foot.
And two pillars should be placed, one under the feet of the patient, and the other under their head; and the pillar placed under the buttocks should be wrapped with wet cloths, so that the patient is not damaged by the pillar being between their thighs, so that the extension toward the lowest part is not hindered.
And each assistant should extend their part, and the doctor with his hand should guide the reduction according to the art.
And when the dislocation is forward, then the leg should be extended more than usual, and according to this measurement, the palm of the doctor's right hand should be placed over the groin, and another assistant should pull that up with their other hand, and with that pulling, extend it toward the lowest part at the knee.
And if the dislocation is backward, then the patient' leg should not be extended toward the lowest part, and it should be elevated above the ground; but it should be placed on a hard surface, just as the leg joint is dislocated to the outside, according to what we have said about its placement on two surfaces; and it should lie on its side and the bandages should be extended, according to what we have said, without pain.
And there should be administration of compression with a table over the area where the joint is located.
So when the reduction is complete according to what we have said — and the sign of the reduction of it is not hidden from you, and it is that you extend two legs, and when you see those angles and the patient stretches their leg and expands it without excuse, then you know that the member according to which it has returned — and then you adjust two thighs and pause with plaster and expand it with a bandage so that the joint is not bent in any of the parts; and bind the leg to rest for three days or four.
Then, cut the ligament and the plaster, and compare one leg to the other.
Now, if you see these wounds in reality, then know that the dislocation is already healed and the patient can walk.
And if you see any cause for softening, then return and plaster that one, and stretch the other according to your first stretching, and leave it for three days.
Then loosen that one, and make that one delay in walking for some days, until he is comfortable.
Chapter 32.
Of the cure of dislocation of the jaw.
The jaw is dislocated in three ways: it is dislocated at the outward parts, and at the inward parts, and at the lower parts more than at the upper parts; and it is not dislocated at the frontward parts.
And the sign of dislocation is that you command the patient to apply his jaw to his thigh; then know that the jaw is dislocated.
And the restoration of all these ways is that you make the patient lie down straight, so that he extend his leg, if he can, on that; adhere your two hands to his face, and place his foot between your feet; and then make adhere your jaw to his palm, and retain those between your teeth over his jaw with strength, and another extends his leg while the jaw returns to its place.
And the sign of reduction is that his thigh adheres to the cushion with light non-labouring.
Then plaster that one and make adhere the leg to the cushion, and then bind those together with a bandage for three or four days, and then loosen those.
And do not use the patient of walking for some days until he is healed and comfortable.
But if the reduction to you is excused, then administer strong extension with ligaments of which in the cure of the hip preceding narrative.
Chapter 33.
Of the cure of the dislocation of the ankle.
The ankle some times is sprained by small removal, and some times it is dislocated according to complement, and the dislocation of it is made either at the inward parts or at the outward parts.
And the sign of the dislocation of it is that you see the ankle swollen proceeding to the part to which it is dislocated.
But the cure of the sprain of it is by slight reduction, and it is that he be extended with facility with hands and be bound while he returns.
But in the cure of it when it is dislocated according to complement, you should make the patient lie down straight, and have one strong and valiant minister of the part behind the jaw of that in the middle place of it.
And then you with your right hand draw the foot of the highest part, and with your left hand of the lowest part of the foot in the place of the ankle.
And then pull the foot to you with your right hand, and then with the left twice, and then extend with the left; and press the foot of the leg with the right beneath the thigh.
And do that two times according as we have counted.
And then press the foot of the leg to the thigh the third time, and you are at the ankle.
Therefore if it returns in one time or two according to this manner, and if you see the foot swollen, it is good; and if not, then repeat the operation on it, for it will return.
But if to you is prohibited the reduction of it by that which we have recommended, then make the patient lie down on his back on earth, and stretch a stake in firm earth, and that box between his thighs, and you already have wrapped a cloth around him so that he does not slide.
And then the minister of it have his thighs, and then another minister extend the leg with their hands or with ligament that lies over the neck of the leg; and then each minister extend against extension of his fellow, and the stake be extended between the thighs of the patient retaining that, so that the body of him is not pulled to the lowest parts beyond his extension.
And then the doctor softens the dislocation with their hands, and another minister have the healthy thigh to the lowest parts, for the dislocation returns with facility.
And therefore when the dislocation returns and is declared to you the health of the reduction of it, then pause plaster and stretch that with ligaments firmly, and bind the leg to the ankle.
And you should fear or keep from the nerves which are behind on the ankle, lest the ligament over that be violent and lead it strongly.
And then leave that for two days or three; and if the ligament is softened, stretch that.
And then loosen that on the third day or the fourth, and forbid the patient to walk for 40 days. But if he is forced to walk before that space, it is not done with security that the dislocation is not dissolved and corrupted, and then that which does not receive cure.
And if there happens to him an abscess with pus, then you minister in the ceding of it that in which our narrative preceded, in another place of cure and of fomentation, while it is suppurative.
Chapter 34.
Of the cure of dislocation of the toes of the feet.
That which is dislocated be swollen with little extension without difficulty; and that which is difficult, beforehand is lighter.
But if the dislocation is in some part of the jaw of the leg, then you make the patient lie down his leg on even ground or on a table, and be standing thus as if he were walking.
And then you stand on your feet, and place your leg over that which protrudes from the joints, and then press that with your leg with strength while it returns, and see that which is swollen and does not appear in the place prominent.
And then pause under the belly of the leg of him a table that takes all the leg, to which are two ends, and then stretch that with decent and firm extension for three days; and then loosen that and make that rest from walking for some days, while it is stretched out and of reduction is assured.
Chapter 35.
Of the species of dislocation that are made by plague or by fracture, or by any other impingement.
When there happens any cause of those, and you are expert in the cure of that and in the restoration of it, many times you succeed after death.
And therefore do not presume upon the cure of it, but that which is expert in the art, long-suffering, compassionate and pitiful, tardy, not hasty nor presumptuous; and use in the beginning of medicines that produce suppurative abscesses justly, and let the patient be subject to divine judgement, unless you hope for salvation from perdition, from the wickedness alleviation, and in which appears some hope. And then try as much as you can of it the reduction in the beginning of the cause, before that he receives suppurative abscess.
And then if the member returns according as you wish, then minister regimen which yields suppurative abscess and cures the plague with that which suits him of the gummed parts dried.
And if dislocation is by fracture and impingement happens in the separated bones, then you be expert of that, and do in that what we have said in the simple wickedness of those.
And observe and avoid according to your ability the instrument of fear as I have described it in my sermon; for by doing so you will better serve your Creator, more firmly uphold your glory, and bring greater health to your true body in this life. Thus ends the text of Albucasis, may God bless it. Amen.
